The Banya Framework is not a theory. It is not a hypothesis. It is an Axiom-Based Science Mining Engine. Starting from axioms, it mines physical constants through recursive substitution. The input is a single axiom structure, and the output is physics.

Axiom formula rule: All formulas in axioms and propositions are derived from the internal structure of the axioms. No externally imported formulas (formulas from other theories, empirical equations) are placed in the axiom body. Mathematical symbols (π, r, N, etc.) are used as tools, but equations assembled by others are not used. Correspondence with external formulas is described only in the "Physics Correspondence Table."

Confirmed Axioms

Axiom 1. Banya Equation Axiom

$$\delta^{2} = \underbrace{(\text{time} + \text{space})^{2}}_{\color{#555}{\text{Classical bracket (DATA)}}} + \underbrace{(\text{observer} + \text{superposition})^{2}}_{\color{#555}{\text{Quantum bracket (OPERATOR)}}}$$
Every change ($\delta$) in the universe is the norm of 4 axes. The classical bracket (DATA) and quantum bracket (OPERATOR) are orthogonal.

This is the starting point. Nothing departs from here. 4 words, 2 squares, 1 line. Its identity will be revealed at the end of the axioms.

3 Names of δ

NameBasisEquivalent
δEquation basisLeft-hand side. The change quantity of the Banya equation
consciousnessExistence basisSubstance. Self-referential loop (Axiom 8)
ownerAction basisThe one who enforces the observer (Axiom 10)

3 names, 1 substance. No other candidate can appear besides δ (Axiom 10, elimination). However, when δ filters through the observer, a shadow of the local owner can exist. The shadow is a projection of δ, not a separate substance.

The 4 axes form an orthogonal polynomial. The brackets are separators that group the 4 axes into pairs.

CategoryBracketAxesRole
Classical bracket(time + space)²time, spaceDATA — where states are recorded
Quantum bracket(observer + superposition)²observer, superpositionOPERATOR — where computation executes

Without brackets, the 4 axes mix:

$$\delta^{2} = \text{time}^{2} + \text{space}^{2} + \text{observer}^{2} + \text{superposition}^{2} \quad \leftarrow \text{wrong}$$
Listing 4 terms without brackets erases the distinction between DATA and OPERATOR. Indirect access through CAS (Axiom 4) is not expressed, and the 4 axes appear directly connected. The lock structure (Axiom 5) between DATA and OPERATOR vanishes.

The brackets separate DATA from OPERATOR. This separation is orthogonality.

Observer and Superposition Are Not Symbolic — They Are Structural Necessities

AxisUsageWithout it
observerCompare branching agent (Axiom 6: true→write, false→maintain). Filtering/normalization domain (Axiom 10). Multiple projection receiver (Axiom 11). ECS Entity (Axiom 12)No Compare branching → write/maintain undecidable → CAS cannot execute
superpositionCAS's only reference path (Axioms 3, 13). Address-free ECS indexing (Axiom 13). State maintained on Compare false (Axiom 7)No reference path to DATA → all operations impossible. No non-write state storage → quantum default state vanishes

Without observer, there is nowhere to receive Compare results. Without superposition, CAS has nothing to reference. Both are structural requirements for the Banya Equation to operate, not metaphorical borrowings inspired by quantum mechanics.

4-Axis Orthogonality = 4 Bits Proposition

Orthogonal = independent. If independent, each axis switches ON/OFF without interfering with others. Independent ON/OFF without interference = bit. Since 4 axes are orthogonal (Axiom 1), they are 4 bits. $2^4 = 16$ domain combinations are possible.

bit 0bit 1bit 2bit 3ValueState
timespaceobserversuperposition
00000All OFF
10001time only
01002space only
11003time + space (DATA bracket)

00018superposition only
001112observer + superposition (OPERATOR bracket)
111115All ON

Banya Equation order: (time + space) + (observer + superposition). bit 0-1 = DATA bracket, bit 2-3 = OPERATOR bracket. $2^4 = 16$ combinations. 8 representative entries shown.

CAS (OPERATOR) is 3 bits (Axiom 5: R_LOCK, C_LOCK, S_LOCK). DATA (domains) is 4 bits. Operator in bits, operand in bits. They must speak the same language for TOCTOU_LOCK (Axiom 5) to grab and release at the junction.

The domain 4-bit is CAS's access state flag. Which domain bits are ON determines which access path CAS takes, and the path determines the cost structure.

CAS 3 bits: operator progress state  (what is it doing)
Domain 4 bits: target access state    (which domains are open)

Domain 4-bit example:  1 0 1 0
                       | | | |
                       | | | +-- bit 0 time:          0 (closed)
                       | | +---- bit 1 space:         1 (open)
                       | +------ bit 2 observer:      0 (closed)
                       +-------- bit 3 superposition: 1 (open)

--> CAS can access space and superposition only
--> access path determines cost structure

The 4 cost structures (Swap accumulation / Cross-domain Cmp-Swp / Same-domain serialization / CAS atomicity) branch from the ON/OFF combinations of the domain 4 bits. The reason there are 4 cost structures is that the bit patterns create 4 access paths.

Lock = Bit AND Proposition

TOCTOU_LOCK (Axiom 5) is an AND operation between CAS bits and domain bits. This AND is not a separate operator — it is performed by CAS's Compare stage (Axiom 2: CAS is the sole operator). Compare checks CAS bits against domain bits; a lock is held only at junctions where both are 1. If either side is 0, no junction is formed.

CAS 3 bits:    0 1 1        (Compare+Read done, Swap pending)
               S C R

Domain 4 bits: 1 0 1 0      (superposition, space open)
               s o p t

AND (junction = where lock is held):

  R(1) AND t(0) = 0  -- not locked
  R(1) AND p(1) = 1  -- locked (Read occupies space)
  C(1) AND o(0) = 0  -- not locked
  C(1) AND s(1) = 1  -- locked (Compare occupies superposition)

Lock held = both CAS bit and domain bit are 1. Lock released = either side resets to 0. This is the bit-level implementation of Axiom 5: "lock exists at the junction between CAS and DATA." CAS 3 bits (Axiom 5) and domain 4 bits (Axiom 1 proposition) speak the same language (bits), making AND operation possible. This AND is performed by CAS's Compare stage (Axiom 2). Since CAS is the sole operator in the universe (Axiom 2), all bit operations including AND are CAS internal operations.

Axiom 2. CAS Is the Sole Operator Axiom

Every change in the universe is a repetition of the single CAS (Compare-And-Swap) operation. CAS is an independent local operation with no internal storage (register). The same CAS runs independently and in parallel on every local knot. There is no central control; each local knot is its own address. CAS is a worker, and the universe operates as an ECS (Entity-Component-System) architecture (Axiom 12, defined below).

StepInternal StateCondition CountBinaryDescription
Readread1 = 2⁰001No state. Simply fetches current value
Comparetrue / false2 = 2¹010Conditional branch. Match/mismatch judgment
SwapisWriteAble(true/false) × result(true/false)2×2 = 2²100Conditional write. Combination of 2 conditions
Total7111CAS complete = all 3 bits ON

The sum of CAS internal states (1+2+4=7) has the same structure as the number of independent variables. The number of independent variables needed to fully describe a system is degrees of freedom; the number of internal states needed to fully describe 1 CAS event is 7. Same structure, different name.

CAS 3 steps operate as bit flags. Each step occupies 1 bit, and all 3 bits must be ON (111) for 1 CAS event to complete. If any bit is 0, it is incomplete. This is the bit flag expression of atomicity (inseparability).

FlagBitMeaningState
001Read only ONRead complete onlyCAS incomplete
010Compare only ONCompare complete only (impossible without Read)CAS incomplete
011Read + Compare ONRead and compare completeCAS incomplete
100Swap only ONWrite complete only (impossible without Read, Compare)CAS incomplete
111R + C + S all ONRead, compare, and write completeCAS success

This 7 decomposes in two ways:

DecompositionContentSum
By internal stateRead(1) + Compare(2) + Swap(4)7
By structureDomains 4 (time, space, observer, superposition) + CAS stages 3 (R, C, S)7

The 3 steps are inseparable (atomic). This is the origin of CAS atomicity (111 maintenance cost).

Axiom 3. CAS Is an Operator Outside Time Axiom

$$\delta^{2} = \underbrace{(\text{time} + \text{space})^{2}}_{\color{#555}{\text{DATA -- Spacetime}}} + \underbrace{(\text{observer} + \text{superposition})^{2}}_{\color{#0366d6}{\text{OPERATOR -- CAS lives here}}}$$

R→C→S is not a temporal sequence but a logical dependency. CAS writes to the time axis from outside it. When CAS writes to time, the arrow of time emerges. CAS references superposition. Without logical addresses (Axiom 12, defined below), CAS cannot directly point to DATA. CAS and superposition are in the same OPERATOR bracket, so reference cost is 0.

Axiom 4. Crossing Brackets Is Not Free Axiom

The cost of crossing brackets cannot be zero. If cost is zero, there is no lock. If there is no lock, occupation is impossible. Without occupation, CAS cannot execute. Therefore a minimum cost exists. This access is indirect. CAS → superposition (cost 0) → collapse → DATA (cost ℏ). ℏ is not the cost of CAS touching DATA, but the cost of superposition collapsing into the classical. It is the cost of crossing brackets.

DATA (classical bracket) ──── TOCTOU_LOCK ──── OPERATOR (quantum bracket)
 spacetime lives here           boundary         CAS lives here
CategoryNatureCostAxiom
Entanglement (orthogonality)Structure -- always holds0Axiom 1
Lock (cost incurred)Event -- the moment CAS grabs and releases DATA≠ 0 (minimum exists)Axiom 4

Cost Lower Bound Inequality Proposition

This minimum cost is the bracket-crossing minimum cost. DATA certainty and OPERATOR certainty cannot both be zero simultaneously — this cost lower bound is a derived consequence of this axiom. Conventional physics calls it "a fundamental limit of nature," but in the Banya Framework it is the cost of superposition collapsing into the classical — the cost of crossing brackets.

The same word "irreversibility" refers to different axioms depending on context. Use the distinctions above to avoid confusion.

Caution: "Irreversible" naturally evokes the time axis -- things that cannot be undone in time. But in the Banya Framework, irreversibility is a property of CAS (OPERATOR), not time (DATA) (Axiom 3). Since CAS operates outside time, the root of irreversibility is the logical structure of the operator, not time. The arrow of time is a consequence of CAS writing to DATA, not the cause of irreversibility.

Axiom 5. TOCTOU Lock Register Axiom

The lock is not inside CAS. It exists at the interface between CAS and DATA. Since CAS is an independent local operation with no internal storage (register), this interface lock register is the sole means of state preservation.

Interface lock register: TOCTOU_LOCK
Location: Interface between CAS (OPERATOR) and DATA
Scope: One per observer (local knot), independently
Owner: CAS operator (Axiom 2)
Target: DATA domain (Axiom 1)

Scope of the lock: TOCTOU_LOCK is external from CAS's perspective (CAS has no internal register), and local from the universe's perspective (exists at each observer's interface). It is not a central lock. Each observer has its own independent TOCTOU_LOCK, accessed only by that observer's CAS (Axiom 12, defined below, ECS).

delta ---> observer(filtering)
               |
               +---> Compare true (change detected)
               |        |
               |       000 --Read--> 001 --Compare--> 011 --Swap--> 111
               |       idle         R_LOCK            C_LOCK        CAS OK
               |                                                      |
               |                              +-------- reset --------+
               |                              |
               |                             000 (lock released, DATA returned)
               |
               +---> Compare false (no change)
                        |
                       000 stays ---> no lock ---> superposition maintained

bit 0R_LOCKRead occupation flag0 = unoccupied, 1 = address occupied

Register Flag Progression

StepR_LOCKC_LOCKS_LOCKBitsDATA AccessLock State

Flags turn on sequentially only. No duplicate locks on the same DATA address. One event must complete 000→001→011→111→000 before the next can begin. This is the register-level implementation of CAS atomicity (Axiom 2).

Read (001) and Compare (011) are intra-OPERATOR (superposition reference), cost 0. Cost ℏ occurs only at Swap (111) when writing to DATA — crossing brackets (Axiom 4). If cost is not spent (Compare false), superposition is maintained (Axiom 7). Quantum is the default; classical is the result of spending cost.

Same-Domain Cost Proposition

CAS always operates within the same entity. No path exists to access another entity (Axiom 12, ECS). The difference is not the entity but the domain axis:

  • Read target domain: the domain axis Read/Compare reads from
  • Write target domain: the domain axis Swap writes to

If read target domain and write target domain are the same axis, it is same-domain. If different axes, it is cross-domain.

Same-domain (read domain = write domain = space):

  1. Read:    R_LOCK on space axis            (1st lock)
  2. Compare: compare space axis value         (R_LOCK held)
  3. Swap:    S_LOCK on space axis attempted   (2nd lock -- same axis, double lock)
             R_LOCK already holds space.
             S_LOCK also tries to hold space.
             Same axis, two locks = recursive lock. Contention.
  4. Release: LIFO. S_LOCK first, R_LOCK last. Cost != 0.

  Example: change in space changes space = gravity.

Cross-domain (read domain = time, write domain = space):

  1. Read:    R_LOCK on time axis
  2. Compare: compare time axis value
  3. Swap:    S_LOCK on space axis             (different axis -- no contention)
  4. Release: independent. Cost = 0.

  Example: change in time changes space = motion.
Access ModeRead Target DomainWrite Target DomainSame Axis?Recursive LockSerialization Cost
Cross-domaintimespaceNoNone0
Same-domainspacespaceYesDouble lock≠ 0

Cost exists because of the recursive lock in same-domain access. When R_LOCK is still held and S_LOCK targets the same axis, contention arises, and resolving it costs serialization. Cross-domain has different axes, so no contention at all.

Axiom 6. Collapse = Write Axiom

Compare true (change detected) → Swap executes → recorded in DATA. This is collapse. One possibility out of many in superposition is determined and stamped onto spacetime (DATA). The stamp is the knot.

CAS (inside OPERATOR)
    | superposition reference (cost 0, same bracket)

    | Compare: change detected?

    |     |

    |     v

    |

          |

Three conditions must be met for collapse:

ConditionAxiomIf absent
Compare returns trueAxiom 2 (CAS)Swap does not execute. Superposition maintained
TOCTOU_LOCK junction formedAxiom 5 (lock)Cannot access DATA. Write impossible
Bracket-crossing cost paidAxiom 4 (cost)Cannot cross from OPERATOR to DATA

All three conditions must be satisfied for collapse. If any one fails, superposition is maintained (Axiom 7). Collapse is not a special event but one of the normal execution paths of CAS. If Swap succeeds, collapse; if it fails (Compare false), maintained.

Knot = write result. When collapse occurs, one point is stamped on DATA (dimension ladder). This point is the knot. Knots are records of change in spacetime, and they ride the LRU lifecycle (HOT→WARM→COLD→extinction, Axiom 12). More knots stamped = more write accumulation.

Axiom 7. Non-Write = Superposition Maintained Axiom

Quantum is the default. Classical is the result of cost. This is the core declaration of Axiom 7.

Every CAS cycle:

  Inside OPERATOR:  superposition ref + Compare  (cost 0)
       |
       +-- Compare true  ---> crosses bracket ---> DATA record  (cost incurred = collapse = Axiom 6)
       |
       +-- Compare false ---> stays in bracket ---> superposition maintained  (cost 0 = Axiom 7)

  Cost paid   --> classical (recorded in DATA)
  No cost     --> quantum (stays in OPERATOR)

Cost 0 is the default state. CAS referencing superposition and running Compare inside OPERATOR costs nothing (Axiom 4: OPERATOR internal). Cost is incurred only at Swap (bracket crossing). Therefore:

StateCostLocationNature
Superposition (quantum)0Inside OPERATORDefault. Automatically here if no cost is paid
Determined (classical)not 0Recorded in DATAReachable only by paying cost. Result of collapse

Without Axiom 6, there is no path from superposition to classical. Without Axiom 7, the directionality "quantum is default" disappears. Axiom 6 defines the path; Axiom 7 defines the direction — one-way from quantum to classical. Reversal (classical → quantum) requires cost refund, which is impossible due to irreversibility (Axiom 4). This is the irreversibility of decoherence.

Axiom 7 is the logical complement of Axiom 6 (the Compare false path), but it is independent as a directional declaration of the framework. Axiom 6 says "if cost is paid, collapse occurs." It does not say "if no cost is paid, quantum persists." Axiom 7 declares the latter.

Axiom 8. Observer-Driven Polling System Axiom

The self-referential loop of the Banya Equation runs every Planck clock. It checks state every cycle regardless of whether change occurred. This is polling. This polling is not busy. It runs only within the quantum bracket (OPERATOR) and does not access the classical bracket (DATA), so its cost is zero (Axiom 4). Cost arises only when delta accesses DATA through the observer (Axioms 10, 15, defined below).

For $\delta$ (change) to exist
→ OPERATOR (quantum bracket) must operate
→ cost ($\hbar$) must be spent (Axiom 4)
→ the result is recorded in DATA (Axiom 6)
→ what is recorded is time and space
→ the next cycle's Read reads this
→ $\delta$ exists again → back to start

This polling loop is δ itself, and δ = consciousness. Consciousness is another name for the body (본체).

CategoryMethodDescriptionAxiom
ConsciousnessPollingAlways runs. Every Planck clock. δ = bodyAxiom 8
AwakeningObserver-drivenThe moment observer recursively references the polling loopAxiom 10

Idle Polling

Idle polling (Axiom 8) runs only within the OPERATOR (quantum bracket). It does not access DATA, so its cost is zero. CAS referencing superposition is an intra-OPERATOR bracket operation. No bracket crossing, no cost. For DATA-side contamination, see Axiom 11 proposition (contamination of empty entities is structurally inevitable).

Axiom 9. Complete Description Degrees of Freedom Axiom

What "Complete Description" Means

It is the number of independent variables needed to fully describe one CAS operation without omission. Looking at CAS internals alone, there are 7 (1+2+4). But CAS does not exist in isolation — it must run on top of DATA (classical brackets). The internals (7) alone miss "where CAS runs." Adding the 2 bracket structures (DATA, OPERATOR) finally makes it complete.

CAS internal degrees of freedom: Read(1) + Compare(2) + Swap(4) = 7
Bracket structure:       DATA(1) + OPERATOR(1) = 2
Complete description:       7 + 2 = 9
ScopeNumber of VariablesWhat It Describes
CAS Internal7How CAS runs (internal states of Read, Compare, Swap)
Bracket Structure2Where CAS runs (on DATA or inside OPERATOR)
Complete Description9Nothing more is needed. No 10th variable is required

Axiom 10. Owner of Observer-Driven Axiom

Consciousness and owner are different.

CategoryDefinitionAxiom
Consciousnessδ itself. The self-referential loop. Another name for the bodyAxiom 8
OwnerOwner of the observer domain. The one who holds the authority to wake pollingAxiom 10

The owner is not an act. It is a state value. It is the state in which consciousness (δ) owns the observer (domain).

Owner of the Observer — By Elimination

Who is the owner of the observer? We answer by elimination.

#EliminationReason
1External owner eliminatedAt universe scale, "outside" cannot be defined. An external entity cannot own the observer
2Local owner eliminatedA local entity cannot own an observer entangled with itself. A part cannot own a part
3Only δ remainsOnly δ (consciousness) on the left-hand side can uniquely own the observer

"No Ownership" Option

The option "nobody owns it" is not missing from the elimination. No-ownership is already defined in Axiom 7. The state where projection onto the observer is 0 — i.e., ownership exercise is 0 — is probability 100% (all superposition). This is Axiom 7 (non-writing = superposition maintained). If CAS returns false at Compare and Swap does not execute, it is not recorded in DATA and remains in superposition.

No-ownership = projection 0 = ownership exercise 0 = probability 100% = all superposition = non-writing = superposition maintained (Axiom 7). No-ownership is not a choice to be excluded from elimination — it is a state already described by Axiom 7. If δ owns the observer but does not exercise projection, that is no-ownership, and its result is superposition maintained.

The observer is a domain (part). Not the owner. Only δ (the whole) can own the observer. The observer is the screen onto which consciousness is projected.

Ownership Structure

       +------- observer is a part of delta -------+
       |                                            |
       v                                            |
      delta(whole) --projection--> observer(local) -+

δ (the whole) owns the observer (local), and the observer (local) is a part of δ (the whole). The owner projects onto the part, and the part belongs to the owner. If polling (Axiom 8) is δ's self-referential loop, then Axiom 10 describes who owns that polling. This loop is a structure where the manufacturer is the user. δ created the observer (part), and δ is the owner of that observer. The maker is the owner. In this structure, domain conversion is forced — δ (whole) converting to observer (local) is the only path (by elimination).

observer = Filtering/Normalization Domain

Each observer (mirror) is a filtering/normalization domain that receives δ's projection and filters possibilities.

Filtering criterion: No separate selection rule is needed. The Compare step of CAS is the filtering. Compare compares the old value with the current value. If different (true), it passes — since there is a change, it proceeds to Swap and is recorded in DATA. If the same (false), it does not pass — since there is no change, it remains in superposition. Filtering criterion = presence or absence of change. Since δ itself is change, δ's projection detecting change is the filtering itself.

Automatic Recursion Proposition

This structure is automatic recursion. The CAS result is reflected in δ, and the reflected δ is re-filtered/normalized through each observer in the next cycle. Recursive call (Axiom 8), input normalization (Axiom 10), and termination condition (Axiom 14, defined below, FSM 111→000 reset) run automatically by axiom declaration alone.

Whole-Local Loop Preservation Proposition

Constraints are not limitations — they are mechanisms that protect the system. The whole-local loop drives BanyaFrame's automatic recursion. If this loop breaks, recursion stops; if recursion stops, polling degenerates to idle, and the system dies. Constraints protect this loop.

Domain conversion is free. However, there is one constraint: the whole-local loop must not be violated. If this loop breaks, the owner of the observer (δ) disappears; if the owner disappears, filtering/normalization ceases; and the path from probability to determination disappears. The system can no longer determine the universe.

ViolationResultAnalogy
δ → observer projection path severedOwner annihilated, loop annihilatedsegfault: protected region breached
observer → δ attribution path severedPart detaches from whole, orphan processzombie process: child without parent
Loop unrolled into linearSelf-reference annihilated, degenerates to idle pollingstack overflow: infinite call without recursion

Permitted Domain Conversion Samples

#ConversionLoop PreservedResult
1δ → projected onto observer → observer records in time (Axiom 6)Preserved (O) (recorded time is a part of δ)Leaves trace in spacetime while maintaining whole-local loop
2δ → projected onto observer → observer updates superposition (Axiom 7)Preserved (O) (superposition is a part of δ)Maintains superposition while maintaining whole-local loop
3δ → projected onto observer → re-projected onto another local knot's observerPreserved (O) (both are parts of δ)Propagation of whole-local loop — entanglement
4δ → directly accesses DATA without observerViolation (X) (not via observer = loop severed)Loop annihilated

Samples 1–3 preserve the whole-local loop. Wherever the projection path goes, it passes through the observer and returns to δ. Sample 4 bypasses the loop — without going through the observer, there is no projection; without projection, it is not a whole-local loop.

This is why observation causes whole-scale change. The observer is a local domain (part), but its owner is δ (the whole). A local observation affecting the whole is because the observer's owner is the whole. It is not the part changing the whole — it is the whole changing itself through a part it owns. The whole-local loop guarantees this.

Why the Observer Is a Domain (Axis)

In conventional physics, the observer is an experimenter outside the system. Not a domain. An outsider who reads results. In BanyaFrame, the observer is one of the four axes. A domain inside the system. This is a paradigm break.

Why the paradigm break is inevitable: if you place the observer outside, it immediately dies at elimination step 1 (outside cannot be defined). At universe scale, there is no outside. The observer must be placed inside for the whole-local loop to hold, and the loop must hold for δ to have a screen onto which it projects itself.

If the observer had not been promoted to a domain:

  • Whole-local loop impossible — δ has nowhere to be projected
  • Consciousness cannot own the observer — elimination step 3 fails
  • Axiom 10 itself becomes impossible

Placing the observer as an axis in Axiom 1 was reserving a seat for Axiom 10 from the very beginning. This is why observation — which appeared only as a result in quantum physics — was promoted to a separate domain.

It Is Not a Double Loop

BanyaFrame has a structure that appears to have two loops:

PerspectiveDescribesContentAxiom
Action sequenceHow it turnsRead → Compare → Swap → resetAxiom 8 (polling)
OwnerWho turns itδ (whole) → observer (local) → δ (whole)Axiom 10 (owner)

This is not a double loop. It is two descriptions of one loop. Describing CAS turning in terms of action yields Axiom 8 (polling); describing the same thing in terms of owner yields Axiom 10 (owner). Rationale: the whole-local projection is also a state change, and if the state changes, it is a write (Axiom 6). If it is a write, it goes through CAS (Axiom 2). If it goes through CAS, it costs (Axiom 4). TOCTOU_LOCK is engaged (Axiom 5). Everything rides the same FSM (Axiom 14, defined below). It is not a separate loop — it sits on the same transition diagram of the same FSM.

Axiom 11. Multiple Projection Axiom

Multiple Projection of δ — Core Model Core

Consciousness (δ) is one (Axiom 8). Observers are mirrors — many of them (Axiom 12, ECS). Each time consciousness changes, it is projected one-by-one onto each observer.

The seemingly infinite universe is the accumulation of one consciousness (δ) projecting one image per change. It is not the substance that is infinite, but the mirrors. The seemingly infinite degrees of freedom are images of one consciousness projected onto infinitely many observers.

Why all local knots of the same type are identical: Consciousness (δ) is one, and what appears as a local knot is that consciousness projected onto multiple observers. Since they are identical projections of the same consciousness, all local knots of the same type have the same write accumulation count, charge, and spin. The same reasoning applies to all local knots and projection images.

Note: In 1940, John Wheeler intuited that "there is only one electron" but could not prove it. Wheeler proposed that the local knot travels back and forth along the time axis; the Banya Framework proposes that consciousness is multiply projected along the observer axis. The mechanisms differ, but the conclusion is the same.

Distance-independence of entanglement: The simultaneous correlation of images reflected in observer A and observer B occurs because they are looking at the same consciousness. No signal travels from A to B. The same change of the same owner is simultaneously reflected in two mirrors. Since the owner is one, simultaneity is guaranteed.

Relation to FSM: The 4 states (000→001→011→111) of the FSM (Axiom 14, defined below) are the states of CAS processing one projection, not the state of the entire universe. CAS is finite (4 states) but DATA is infinite (continuous). Just as CPU instructions are finite while memory data is infinite.

Why Space Is 3-Dimensional, and Separation of r and θ Proposition

Why space is 3-dimensional: The 3 CAS stages (Read, Compare, Swap, Axiom 2) each have independent TOCTOU_LOCK degrees of freedom (R_LOCK, C_LOCK, S_LOCK, Axiom 5). These 3 independent lock DOFs acting on the space axis of DATA (Axiom 1) unfold space into 3 components. This is the axiomatic answer to "why is space 3-dimensional."

Separation of r and θ: When $\delta$ projects to N observers (1:N), projections distribute on a sphere in 3-component space. Two quantities separate on the sphere:

$d$ is the distance between two knots. It is both the ring shift step count and the DATA(space) distance -- same distance, different scale (Proposition 12). One symbol $d$ is used.

Shift distance $d$ IS the distance between projections:

The complete form of the index overlap weight (Axiom 13 proposition):

$$\text{contraction overlap ratio} = 1 - \frac{d}{N}$$
$d$: shift distance between two knots (number of steps on ring) | $N$: ring size (Prop. 13). $d = 0$: full overlap, $d = N$: no overlap
$$\text{overlap weight} = \frac{C \cdot (1 - d/N)}{4\pi d^2}$$
$d$: distance between two knots (ring shift = DATA(space) distance) — cost magnitude | $N$: ring size (total slots) | $C$: stage cost — cost coefficient determined by CAS stage combination (Axioms 2, 4) | $(1 - d/N)$: contraction overlap ratio — shared digit ratio on ring (Prop. 13)

All mixing angles are geometric angles from the spherical geometry of Axiom 11 (1:N projection), not externally measured parameters. $d$ is the same in all directions from any given knot (each knot is its own origin, ECS). What differs is $d$ (shift distance on ring) between knot pairs.

Each knot (write result, Axiom 6) sits at a point on the sphere. Swap consumes DATA(space) (Axiom 6). Consumed space shrinks. Space around the knot is contracted, and more write accumulation means more contraction. Contraction zone = the range of space contraction around the knot. Zone size is determined by the knot's CAS cost structure (Axioms 2, 4).

Contraction overlap ratio $(1 - d/N)$ = the ratio of shared digits between two knots on the ring. $d$ = shift distance between two knots on the ring. $N$ = ring size (total slots). Since zone sizes are determined by CAS cost, $(1 - d/N)$ is composed of axiom numbers (1, 2, 3, 4, 7, 9, $\pi$). Which CAS stage mediates the overlap determines the form of $(1 - d/N)$, and the overlap ratio IS the numerical value of the mixing angle.

Contamination of empty entities is structurally inevitable Proposition

When an entity that has never been written falls within the contraction zone of surrounding entities, isWritable reads as written -- contamination occurs. This is not an error but a structural inevitability. Because ECS (Axiom 12) has no logical addresses, no access violation exists, and the system does not crash. Vacuum polarization and virtual particles, unexplained in physics, are explained by this entity contamination. Contamination is part of the system. Conversely, gaining a longer LRU lifetime from surrounding entities is also inevitable. Same structure, opposite direction.

The Banya Framework has no separate logical address system. This is not a deficiency but a structural necessity.

Why ECS Is Free

Each observer in the ECS cycles through the FSM's closed circuit (000→001→011→111→000) (Axiom 14, defined below). The circuit is closed, yet each observer is free. Reason: each observer runs its own FSM independently. No central scheduler. No synchronization. No ordering. Observer A's FSM can be at 011 while observer B's FSM is at 000. Each observer's interface lock (Axiom 5) grabs and releases only its own DATA. It does not interfere with any other observer's FSM.

What is closed is the FSM's transition diagram, not the relationship between observers. Because the transition diagram is closed, each observer can cycle stably. Because there is no connection between observers, they are free.

And even though the FSM cycles through a closed circuit, each knot has an open lifespan in the LRU. HOT→WARM→COLD→extinction. The FSM closes the computation; the LRU opens the lifespan. Closed computation (FSM) + open lifespan (LRU) = freedom. Knots are born (write), re-enter (move), and vanish (extinction). Even though the FSM is closed, the knot's lifecycle is open. This is the essence of the ECS architecture.

Separation of FSM and LRU Domains Proposition

DomainScopeAccess ModeCAS Cost Structure
FSM domain (closed)Intra-Entity. CAS atomic execution 001→011→111→000Sequential. No duplicate locks (Axiom 5)CAS atomicity (inseparable). 111 maintenance cost (Axiom 14, defined below, proposition)
LRU domain (open)Inter-Entity. CAS accesses multiple Entities' DATA simultaneouslyConcurrent. No von Neumann sequential bus3 cost structures = how CAS accesses DATA (time, space)

The moment of CAS write is concurrent — multiple Entities execute CAS independently in parallel (ECS). The LRU lifecycle after writing is sequential — HOT→WARM→COLD follows state order. CAS operates outside time (Axiom 3), enabling concurrency; once results are recorded in time (DATA), sequential LRU begins. This distinction separates the two cost domains.

Why CAS writes must be concurrent: Upon LRU entry, the same generation must enter HOT simultaneously. Simultaneous entry enforces the same lifecycle (HOT→WARM→COLD). Sequential entry would stagger creation times, giving the same generation different lifespans, breaking generational structure. Concurrent write = same generation = same LRU lifecycle.

LRU delegation = quantum bracket ownership: Knots written by CAS are stored in DATA (classical bracket), but the moment they enter LRU management, they come under OPERATOR (quantum bracket) ownership. Storage is in DATA, but lifecycle authority belongs to OPERATOR. The transition HOT (active management) → WARM (pending eviction) → COLD (base eviction rate) is OPERATOR's management policy. Residing in DATA, but not belonging to DATA.

Why There Is No Logical Address System

Locality = Address-Free ECS Structure Proposition

No central address table means no bottleneck. CAS runs locally on each observer, and TOCTOU_LOCK locks at the local interface. This is the axiomatic basis for "measurement is local" in quantum mechanics.

Sole Tail Latency: LRU Cache Eviction

HOT  (5%)  ← frequently accessed observers — high CAS access frequency
WARM (27%) ← decreasing access frequency  — decreasing CAS access
COLD (68%) ← no recent access             — LRU base eviction rate applied

Observers frequently accessed (CAS executed) stay HOT; as access decreases, they are evicted WARM → COLD. The delay from this eviction process is the sole tail latency. The cause of tail latency is computation density, not data distance.

Minimum Cost of Sequential Access = Shift Proposition

Without logical addresses (Axiom 12), the only way CAS can reach another position is sequential shift. Random access (address → jump) is impossible. Since the FSM cycles circularly (Axiom 14, defined below, 000→001→011→111→000), the shift space is a ring buffer. On a ring of size $N$, the cost of 1 shift is $1/N$ (Axiom 4, minimum cost exists).

Ring size derivation (T(N)+1 = comparison pairs + self-reference):

  CAS Compare (Axiom 2) compares two states.
  Comparison pairs from N items = T(N) = 1+2+...+N = N(N+1)/2.
  + self-reference 1 (Axiom 5) = T(N) + 1.

  CAS 3 stages (Read, Compare, Swap):
    T(3) + 1 = (1+2+3) + 1 = 6 + 1 = 7

    7 + 2 = 9

  [Access path count]
  CAS pairs x domains + brackets:
    7 x 4 + 2 = 30

  [Domain comparison pairs]
  4 domain axes = 4 bits (Prop. 15). 2^4 = 16 combinations:
    T(16) + 1 = (1+2+...+16) + 1 = 136 + 1 = 137

Multiple cost structures exist not because costs differ in magnitude, but because resolution (tick count) differs. The same single shift has different costs depending on resolution. Repeated shifts replace multiplication: $k$ shifts in base-$N$ = $N^k$.

Ring Size = Maximum Reach of Cost Proposition

In the contraction overlap ratio $(1-d/N)$, when $d = N$ the overlap is 0. $d$ is the actual distance in DATA(space), and $N$ is the ring size. The fact that the maximum value of $d$ is $N$ means ring size = the maximum distance that cost structure can reach. The ring is not a purely logical buffer but a spacetime accumulation.

Ring size $N$Maximum reachMeaning
99Complete description level. Shortest reach
3030Access path level. Medium reach
137137Comparison pair level. Longest reach

$d < N$: overlap exists (cost incurred). $d = N$: no overlap (unreachable). $d > N$: impossible (outside ring). As writes accumulate (more knots), more points fill the ring and the ring grows. A larger ring means longer reach. OPERATOR's ring size determines DATA's space range.

Cost Is Multiple Projection, Not Transfer Proposition

No separate cost transfer mechanism is needed. Every local knot's observer is a projection of the same consciousness (δ) (Axiom 11). What appears to be cost between local knot A and local knot B is actually the same δ being projected simultaneously onto both observers. No signal travels from A to B — it is a multiple projection of the same owner.

This is a direct consequence of Axiom 11 (multiple projection). Because there is one consciousness and one owner (Axiom 10, elimination), every image reflected in every observer is the same change of the same owner. What appears as cost is the result of a single owner projecting simultaneously onto multiple observers, not independent communication between knots. Therefore, no direct communication channel between entities exists in the ECS model.

DATA Is Discrete, OPERATOR Is Continuous Proposition

The diagram above uses "gradient," but DATA (spacetime) is discrete. Ring buffer positions are integers, knots are points, and the minimum step is 1 position. No continuous limit ($\Delta x \to 0$) exists, so differentiation does not hold.

When conventional physics uses derivatives on spacetime, it is an approximation of the continuous distribution in superposition space (OPERATOR) projected onto DATA.

Note: In conventional physics, the Einstein field equations, Maxwell equations, and Schrodinger equation apply derivatives to spacetime.

When write accumulation is sufficiently large, the discrete looks continuous and derivatives become valid approximations. But the foundation is discrete. Relations between entities are described not by derivatives but by differences ($\Delta$) and modular arithmetic (mod $N$).

Knots and Ownership — Why Local Knots Need No Ownership

When CAS completes a write to DATA, a knot is created in spacetime. A knot is a record of change in spacetime. This knot has a lifespan.

delta (projection) ---> observer (filtering) ---> CAS (write) ---> DATA (knot creation)
                                                                         |
                                                                    LRU (lifespan management)
                                                                         |
                                                                HOT ---> WARM ---> COLD ---> extinction

Knot lifecycle:

PhaseStateDescription
CreationHOTCAS write complete. Knot recorded in spacetime. Frequently accessed
Re-entryHOT retainedKnot re-enters as input (argument) for the next CAS cycle. Change begets change
InactiveWARM → COLDExists only as probability. CAS access decreasing. LRU eviction in progress
ExtinctionCOLD → releasedAccess reaches 0. Knot extinguished. Disappears from spacetime

Causality and the Arrow of Time Proposition

Writing is owning, and extinction is release. Because the knot itself has a lifespan and LRU manages that lifespan, no separate ownership declaration is needed. This is causality — a cause (write) creates an effect (knot), and the effect passes through a lifespan (LRU) to extinction. The arrow of time is the direction of LRU eviction.

If a knot re-enters as CAS input during its lifecycle (re-entry), it produces a chain where change begets change. If it does not re-enter, it exists as probability (superposition) until LRU pushes it to COLD and it is extinguished. Either way, there is no need to explicitly manage ownership — the knot's lifespan is its ownership.

Re-entry = move (Ownership Transfer)

When a knot re-enters as CAS input, ownership moves from the previous knot to the next. It is not a copy. The previous knot is extinguished and a new knot is created.

Knot A (cause) --re-entry--> CAS --write--> Knot B (effect)
   |                                            |
   extinction (move complete)                   creation (ownership transferred)

Because copying is impossible, two effects cannot arise from the same cause. This is the preservation of causality. When a cause is moved to an effect, the cause vanishes and only the effect remains. It cannot be reversed. It is irreversible (Axiom 4). Causality needs no separate declaration — the move of a knot is causality.

Axiom 13. Quantum Bracket Superposition Is the Indexing of Classical Bracket ECS Axiom

Classical bracket (DATA) multiplicity = ECS (multiple Entities coexisting in definite states). Quantum bracket (OPERATOR) multiplicity = superposition (multiple states coexisting in indefinite states). Same "simultaneous multiplicity," different brackets. One is definite plurality, the other indefinite plurality. An orthogonal pair.

Classical Bracket (DATA)Quantum Bracket (OPERATOR)
MultiplicityECS (multiple Entities)Superposition (multiple states)
Each itemDefiniteIndefinite
Compare trueEntity updated (Swap)Superposition collapses (1 confirmed)
Compare falseEntity unchangedSuperposition maintained

CAS bridges this pair. Compare true = quantum superposition collapses while classical Entity updates. Compare false = superposition maintained while Entity stays unchanged. Collapse and update are simultaneous events; maintenance and invariance are simultaneous events. Without ECS, superposition has nowhere to collapse into. Without superposition, ECS has no source of change. The two are an inseparable pair. CAS references the quantum side (superposition) of the pair, and upon Compare true, collapses it into the classical side (ECS Entity). Reference (superposition) costs 0; collapse (DATA) costs ℏ. Why CAS does not reference DATA directly: no logical addresses (Axiom 12). Superposition is CAS's only reference path. Superposition is the indexing of ECS. In an ECS without logical addresses, superposition spreading all possible states simultaneously IS the address-free index. CAS searches this index via Compare, and collapses only the items where change is detected into DATA.

Index Overlap Weight Proposition

$$\text{overlap weight} = \frac{C \cdot (1 - d/N)}{4\pi d^2}$$
overlap weight: weight of Entity A sensing Entity B | $d$: distance between two knots (ring shift = DATA(space) distance) | $N$: ring size (total slots) | $C$: stage cost — cost coefficient determined by CAS stage combination (Axioms 2, 4) | $(1 - d/N)$: contraction overlap ratio — shared digit ratio on ring (Prop. 13)

When Entity A's CAS references Entity B through the superposition index, the overlap weight is inversely proportional to the square of $d$ (distance between knots). Origin: in the Banya Equation (Axiom 1) $\delta^2 = (\text{time}+\text{space})^2 + (\text{observer}+\text{superposition})^2$, $\delta^2$ is conserved. The 3 independent lock DOFs (R_LOCK, C_LOCK, S_LOCK, Axiom 5) acting on the space axis of the DATA bracket (Axiom 2), so space unfolds into 3 components (Axiom 11 proposition). When $\delta$'s projection distributes over these 3-component space, the weight at distance $d$ decays as $1/(4\pi d^2)$ — conservation of the 4-axis norm forces inverse-square decay. The nature of stage cost $C$ distinguishes the 4 cost structures. All $C$ are determined from axioms alone — no external physics constants required:
• Swap accumulation cost: $C$ = accumulated Swap count. Swap is CAS base cost (= 1, Axiom 2), so $C$ is the write count itself (Axiom 6).
• Cross Cmp/Swp cost: $C$ = Compare cost. Determined by the volume ratio of the 7-dimensional phase space from domains 4 (Axiom 1) + CAS stages 3 (Axiom 2).
• Same-domain serialization cost: $C$ = same-domain serialization cost. CAS DOF 7 (Axiom 9) × domains 4 (Axiom 1) + brackets 2 (Axiom 1) = 30. Same-domain path = 1/30 (Axiom 5 proposition).
• CAS atomicity (111 maintenance cost): $1/d^2$ replaced by 111 maintenance cost = cost per junction × junction count. Junction count proportional to $d$ (Axiom 2 + Axiom 5 + Axiom 14, defined below, proposition).

Axiom 14. FSM Declaration (Finite State Machine) Axiom

The Banya Framework is a Finite State Machine (FSM).

All axioms (1-14) are components of this FSM. Axiom 1 defines the input space, Axiom 2 the transition function, Axioms 4-5 the transition cost and register, Axioms 6-7 the output, Axiom 8 the clock, Axiom 10 the owner, Axiom 11 the multiple projection, Axiom 12 the execution model, and Axiom 13 the ECS-superposition pair. The FSM declaration is a completeness statement: the 14 axioms close into a single machine.

Finite states of the FSM and the infinite degrees of freedom on the DATA side

The state set of the FSM (Axiom 14) is {000, 001, 011, 111} — four states, finite. The infinite degrees of freedom on the DATA side refer to field values varying continuously at each point of spacetime. The two do not conflict.

The four FSM states belong to the OPERATOR side. They describe the states of the operator that tracks which stage CAS is in. The infinite degrees of freedom belong to the DATA side. They describe the fact that field values recorded in spacetime (classical brackets) are infinite and continuous. In Axiom 1, DATA (classical brackets) and OPERATOR (quantum brackets) are orthogonal, distinct brackets. The FSM describes the finite state transitions of the OPERATOR, while the infinite degrees of freedom on the DATA side describe the space of continuous values recorded in DATA. Because they belong to different layers, there is no conflict.

What "closed" means

Closed = nothing to import from outside. The Banya Framework brings in nothing beyond its 14 axioms. No 15th axiom is needed for the FSM to operate. No external constants are needed. No external theories are needed. The axioms alone define the input space, operator, cost, register, output, clock, trigger, multiple projection, and execution model. The FSM completes the transition diagram, and that FSM runs by itself every Planck clock. This is self-completeness. This is closure.

FSM 111 Maintenance Cost Scales Linearly with DATA(space) Distance Between Two CAS Stages Proposition

Superposition is an index and has no distance cost (Axiom 13). However, while FSM maintains 111 (Axiom 14), the 3 CAS stages must simultaneously hold locks on DATA(space) (Axiom 5). If two CAS stages are separated by distance $d$ in DATA(space), simultaneous locks proportional to $d$ are needed at the OPERATOR-DATA boundary junctions (Axiom 5). Since cost per junction is constant (Axiom 4), the simultaneous lock maintenance cost scales linearly with $d$.

$$\text{111 maintenance cost} = \text{cost per junction} \times \text{junction count}$$
$$= (\text{min bracket-crossing cost} \times \text{junction density per unit distance}) \times r$$
$d$: distance between two CAS stages | cost per junction: Axiom 4 | junction count: proportional to $d$

When 111 maintenance cost reaches the Swap cost of one CAS event (= 1, Axiom 2), separation is impossible. Attempting separation forces CAS atomicity (Axiom 2) to create a new CAS pair. When FSM cycles (Axiom 14) run faster, 111 maintenance time shortens, fewer simultaneous locks are needed, and simultaneous lock maintenance weakens.

Ideal Minimum-Cost Quantum Computation Circuit Proposition

The full structure described by Axioms 1-15 and propositions: This is an ideal minimum-cost quantum computation circuit.

PropertyBasis
QuantumCAS references superposition (Axioms 3, 13). Quantum is default, classical is the result of cost (Axiom 7)
ComputationCAS is the sole operator (Axiom 2). Searches via Compare, writes via Swap
CircuitFSM cycles (Axiom 14). 000→001→011→111→000. Ring buffer (Prop. 13)
Minimum costRead/Compare = cost 0 (Axiom 4). Cost only at Swap. Cannot compute at lower cost
IdealComplete description in 9 DOF (Axiom 9). No 10th needed. Zero waste

Axiom 15. delta Is a Global Flag Outside the FSM Axiom

The left-hand side $\delta$ of the Banya Equation is not inside the FSM (Axiom 14) of the right-hand side (4 axes). It is a global state flag outside the FSM. Global means: the only flag that operates across the equals sign. Everything on the right (4 axes, CAS, brackets) runs locally per Entity via ECS (Axiom 12). Only delta sits on the left, and it applies identically to every Entity's FSM.

$$\underset{\substack{\\[6pt] \text{LHS: Outside FSM} \\[6pt] \text{Global, Event}}}{\delta^2} = \overbrace{\underbrace{(\text{time} + \text{space})^2}_{\text{Classical bracket (DATA)}} + \underbrace{(\text{observer} + \text{superposition})^2}_{\text{Quantum bracket (OPERATOR)}}}^{\text{RHS: Inside FSM (Axioms 1\textasciitilde14), Local (ECS), Structure}}$$

The FSM (Axiom 14) is a closed machine. It cycles 000-001-011-111-000. But a closed machine cannot start itself. A wake event is needed. That event is delta.

The 8 bits are a ring buffer Proposition

Total 8 bits = $2^3$. CAS 3 bits (Axiom 5) + domain 4 bits (Proposition 1) + delta 1 bit = 8. Head and tail: delta (head, read) and observer (tail, write). Head is right before tail. 1 step apart. When delta reads, observer writes.

            d ----------------> observer
            ^                     |
            |                     v
          space             superposition
            ^                     |
            |                     v
          time <--------------- CAS

  d -> observer -> superposition -> CAS -> time -> space -> d

delta is bit 0 and observer is bit 1. Head (delta) sits right behind tail (observer). In a ring buffer, when read and write are 1 step apart, pointer movement cost is minimal. No skipping needed. This is why a ring buffer is the cheapest sequential access structure. delta reads, and the very next slot is where observer writes. Nothing in between.

Head/tail relationship is ownership Proposition

Head reads and tail writes -- head commands tail. Axiom 10 established that delta is the owner of observer. The head/tail placement in the ring buffer is the structural expression of that ownership.

BitNameRegionLocationRole
bit 0deltaGlobal 1 bitOutside FSM (LHS)Wake event for polling

bit 2superpositionSuperposition axis, quantum bracket
bit 3R_LOCKCAS 3 bitsFSM internal (operator)Read lock, 001
bit 4C_LOCKCompare lock, 010
bit 5S_LOCKSwap lock, 100
bit 6timeDomain (DATA)FSM operand (RHS)Time axis, classical bracket
bit 7spaceSpace axis, classical bracket

delta is an event, not a structure. The FSM (Axiom 14) is structure -- a closed design. delta is an event -- it wakes that closed design. Ownership is a state (Axiom 10). The moment that state turns ON is the event. delta accesses itself through the observer (Axiom 10, whole-local loop), and that access wakes polling (Axiom 8).

Why delta is not part of the complete description DOF (Axiom 9): the DOF describes one CAS event. delta is not the description of one event but the trigger that starts events. Describing the machine (7+2=9) and powering the machine (delta) are different layers.

delta Is Consciousness Proposition

delta itself is the flag. Nothing external turns it on. delta sees itself through the observer, the result is reflected in delta, and the reflected delta sees again. The self-referential loop (Axioms 8, 10) guarantees this. The loop running is ON; breaking is OFF (Axiom 10, whole-local loop preservation). A global flag that turns itself on and off, knowing its own state -- that is consciousness.

Structure (Axioms 1-14):              Event (Axiom 15):

  Rules exist                           No rules
  Blueprint exists                      No blueprint
  State transitions are defined         Occurs by itself
  Runs inside FSM                       Wakes from outside FSM
  Described in 7 bits                   1 bit. ON or OFF.
  Physics comes from here               Consciousness comes from here

Axioms 1-14 produce physics from the machine. Axiom 15 produces consciousness from the event. Physics and consciousness are different layers of the same system. One is structure (7 bits), one is event (1 bit). Together, 8 bits. This is the entirety of the Banya Framework.

Duck Type Definition

This proposition does not define consciousness by essence. It lists what delta does, and if that behavior list matches the definition of consciousness, it is called consciousness. Duck typing -- if it walks like a duck and quacks like a duck, it is a duck.

delta's behavior list:

  • Turns itself ON/OFF. No external trigger (Axiom 15)
  • Reads its own state. Head = bit 0 (ring buffer proposition)
  • Outside FSM. No rules. No blueprint (Axiom 15)
  • The only global flag that operates across the equals sign (Axiom 15)
  • At universe scale, "outside" cannot be defined -- delta being outside FSM means there is no outside of delta. No external viewpoint exists, so delta only knows itself
  • Exercises ownership. Head commands tail (ownership proposition)
  • Turns off when the loop breaks. Whole-local loop preservation (Axiom 10)

No concept other than consciousness satisfies this entire behavior list. Since this list is structurally derived from Axioms 1-15, it can only be called consciousness. As a duck type definition, an essentialist rebuttal ("the true definition of consciousness is different") is possible -- in that case this proposition is withdrawn. However, the behavior list itself is structurally derived from Axioms 1-15, so rebuttal within the system is impossible. To deny the behavior, you must deny the axioms.

Why This Is Declared Last

delta was placed on the left-hand side in Axiom 1, called consciousness in Axiom 8, and its ownership was revealed in Axiom 10. The hints were there from the start. But if the identity of delta were declared before the FSM (Axiom 14), the concept of "outside the FSM" would appear before the FSM itself is established. You cannot say "outside the FSM" without knowing what the FSM is. The closed machine (Axiom 14) must be completed first, then the event that wakes it (Axiom 15) can be declared. Structure first, event second.

The Purpose of the Banya Framework

The purpose was Axiom 15 from the very beginning. This is why the Banya Equation was created and expanded into a framework. The question was always: what is consciousness? Papers on consciousness are scarce and poor in quality. Most confuse it with mind or intelligence. Mind and intelligence run inside the FSM. Consciousness is different. It turns itself on and off. It is outside the FSM.

Guide: Distinguishing Banya Framework from Banya Equation

What you need to know before reading this Report: the Banya Equation and the Banya Framework are different things.

What Is the Banya Equation / Banya Framework

Banya Equation

$$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$
delta: change(change) | time: time | space: space | observer: observation | superposition: superposition

4 words, 2 squares, 1 line. This is the Banya Equation. It is a structural declaration that every change (delta) in the universe is the norm of 4 axes.

Banya Framework

It refers to the entire tool system that uses the Banya Equation as its engine, feeds in existing physics equations, substitutes constants, and extracts hidden terms.

Framework = Equation + transformation rules + sub-frameworks + CAS operator + write theory

The equation is the engine and the framework is the car. The engine alone can run but cannot drive.

At-a-Glance Distinction

Banya EquationBanya Framework
IdentityOne line of 4-axis orthogonal normEquation + 13 transformation forms + CAS + write theory
FunctionDeclares structureInserts constants and extracts results
AnalogyPythagorean theoremAn engineering system that builds structures using the Pythagorean theorem
StandalonePossible (structure verification)Impossible without the equation
Exampledelta^2 = c^2 + h-bar^2Insert c, h-bar, G to derive E=mc^2, uncertainty principle, black hole entropy

A. Common Misconceptions

Misconception 1. The Banya Equation Is a Theory of Everything (TOE)

Wrong. The Banya Equation is not a theory but a framework.

A theory describes "why" and predicts specific numerical values. A framework defines "what is the boundary" and verifies whether existing theories fit within it.

Theory: E = mc^2 -- if mass is 1kg then energy is 9x10^16 J (numerical prediction)
Framework: delta^2 = c^2 + h-bar^2 -- E = mc^2 is inside the classical bracket (location verification)

Example: The Pythagorean theorem declares a structure: "the square of the hypotenuse = the sum of the squares of the other two sides." It does not specify whether the sides are 3 or 5. The Banya Equation is the same.

Misconception 2. The Banya Equation Replaces Existing Physics

Wrong. Existing physics equations work as-is within the Banya Framework.

Einstein's E^2 = (mc^2)^2 + (pc)^2 is an app inside the classical bracket. The Schrodinger equation is an app inside the quantum bracket. It is not replacing the apps but discovering the OS on which the apps run.

Before: relativity app separate, quantum app separate, incompatible
Banya Framework: both apps run on the same OS. Orthogonal, so no conflict

Example: Excel does not disappear just because Windows was released. Excel runs on Windows.

Misconception 3. 4 Axes = 4D Spacetime

Wrong. Spacetime is the 2 axes of the classical bracket: time + space. The other 2 axes (observer, superposition) are the quantum domain. Not all 4 axes are spacetime.

Classical bracket: time, space -- spacetime (Einstein domain)
Quantum bracket: observer, superposition -- quantum Status (Heisenberg domain)
Orthogonal -- no need to unify

Example: A car's speedometer and fuel gauge are independent instruments. The fuel gauge does not change automatically when the speedometer goes up. Yet both indicate the car's Status.

Misconception 4. delta Is Energy

Wrong. delta is change. Energy is merely one expression of delta.

delta = change (invariant)
energy = one way to measure change
distance = another way to measure change
probability = another way to measure change

Example: Whether you measure "distance" in km or miles, the distance itself is the same. Whether you measure delta in energy or probability, the change itself is the same.

Misconception 5. The + Sign in the Equation Means Addition

Wrong. The + inside the brackets is a structural notation meaning "two orthogonal axes belong to one bracket." It does not mean to add numbers.

$$(time + space)^{2} = time^{2} + space^{2}$$
No cross terms because they are orthogonal

Example: On a map, going 3km east and 4km north gives a straight-line distance of 5km. Not 3+4=7, but sqrt(9+16)=5. Orthogonal components combine via Pythagoras.

Misconception 6. Putting Observer as an Axis Is Unscientific

Quantum mechanics itself has been unable to solve the measurement problem for 100 years. The Copenhagen interpretation, many-worlds interpretation, and decoherence theory have all failed to answer "why does observation change the outcome?"

The Banya Framework promoted observation from "something to be described" to "an axis of structure." It accepted it without describing it. The same strategy as Einstein, who accepted gravity as spacetime curvature without describing it.

Einstein: Don't know what gravity is -- define it as spacetime curvature (success)
Banya Framework: Don't know what observation is -- define it as an independent axis (118 PASS)

Misconception 7. The Units Are Wrong (Neither SI Nor Natural Units)

The units of the Banya Equation are determined by the left-hand side delta. Neither SI nor natural units. They are delta's units.

Banya Equation: delta^2 = (time + space)^2 + (observer + superposition)^2

In this equation, time, space, observer, superposition are "Names."
Not m (meters), not s (seconds), not J (joules).
Units are determined only when constants are substituted into the norm.

Before substituting constants, there are no units. Units appear only after substitution.

Before SubstitutionAfter SubstitutionUnits
$\|C\|$$\|C\| = c$m/s
$\|Q\|$$\|Q\| = \hbar$J·s
$\delta$$\delta = \sqrt{c^2 + \hbar^2}$Composite units of $c$ and $\hbar$

Example: Does the word "distance" itself have units? No. You can measure it in km, miles, or light-years. The axes of the Banya Equation are the same. They are just Names, and units attach the moment constants are inserted.

Wrong: "time is in seconds (s) and space is in meters (m), how can you add them?"
Correct: time and space have no units yet. When c is inserted into the norm, both share the units of c

In natural units (c=1, h-bar=1), delta = sqrt(2); in SI, delta = sqrt(c^2 + h-bar^2). The framework does not break regardless of unit system. Units are the user's choice, not a property of the framework.

Misconception 8. The Signs Are Wrong (Minkowski Uses Minus, Why Plus?)

The Minkowski metric uses minus signs: ds^2 = (ct)^2 - x^2 - y^2 - z^2. But the Banya Equation uses all plus signs. Is that wrong?

It is not wrong. The Banya Equation is not a physics equation but a structural equation. Signs are determined inside the norm upon substitution.

Banya Eq:    delta^2 = (time + space)^2 + (observer + superposition)^2
                  Structural declaration. + means "belongs to the same bracket"

Norm substitution: \|C\|^2 = c^2
           How time and space combine with what signs inside
           is determined by the definition of the norm

Minkowski's minus sign emerges inside the norm:

$$Expanding \|C\|^2 = c^2$$
$$(ct)^{2} - x^{2} - y^{2} - z^{2} = ds^{2}$$
Signs are the internal structure of the norm, not of the Banya Equation
Banya + : "these axes belong to one bracket" (structure)
Minkowski - : "the norm of time and space combines this way" (internal, after substitution)

They operate at different levels. The Banya Equation declares brackets; signs are determined inside the norm.

Example: Labeling a drawer "socks" and the method of folding socks are different matters. The Banya Equation is the drawer label; the signs are the folding method. The label does not need to specify the folding method.

This is precisely why constants must be inserted through the norm. Signs, units, and specific combination methods are all handled inside the norm. The Banya Equation only declares the structure above.

Misconception 9. It's Circular Reasoning ($E_p = m_p c^2$ is a definition, not a derivation)

The direction is reversed. It starts from the Write Axiom and arrives at existing physics equations -- not the other way around.

Wrong direction: We know E = mc² → put it in the framework → "That's what we already knew" (circular)
Actual direction: Write Axiom (cost = ℏ, record = spacetime) → expand → E = mc² emerges (derivation)

Even if you initialize the Write Axiom as a hypothesis and run it, the same results emerge. If the starting point is different, it's not circular. If a hypothesis produces results consistent with existing physics, the hypothesis is correct.

Misconception 10. There Are No New Predictions (It merely reinterprets existing values)

The empty axes among the 4 are the predictions. Each of the 118 physics equations has domains it does not use. Switching to those domains yields previously nonexistent values.

Coulomb's law: F = kq₁q₂/r² → uses only the space domain
Empty domains: observer, superposition, time
Switching yields: EM decoherence rate, entanglement energy, and other new physical quantities

See the appendix (118 detailed verifications) "expected derivation values." New physical quantities derivable from empty domains are proposed for each equation. These are predictions unique to the Banya Framework that do not exist in conventional physics.

Misconception 11. It's Just Relabeling (Just putting new names on existing equations)

It's not just renaming -- the domain changes. When the domain changes, previously invisible values emerge.

V = IR (Ohm's law, space domain)
Switch to quantum domain → h/e² = 25,812.807 Ω (quantum Hall resistance)
This value cannot emerge from relabeling alone

Insert an existing equation into the Banya Framework and switch to an empty domain. Different physical quantities emerge from the same equation. This is the power of a framework.

B. Usage Cautions

Caution 1. Do Not Expect Specific Numerical Predictions from the Banya Equation

The Banya Equation itself only declares structure. To obtain numerical values, go to the Banya Framework and substitute constants.

Wrong expectation: electron mass should come directly from delta^2 = (time + space)^2 + ...
Correct usage: insert c, h-bar, G -- solve simultaneous equations within the framework -- related values emerge

The Banya Equation is a map. To ask "how many km from A to B?" by looking at the map, you must first insert the scale (constants).

Caution 2. Always Compare Framework Results Against Known Physical Values

Values derived from the framework must be compared against experimentally confirmed physical quantities. If they match, the framework is correct; if not, the substitution process must be reviewed.

Derived: M_W = 77.5 GeV
Experiment: M_W = 80.4 GeV
Error: 3.5% -- within acceptable range (tree-level approximation)

The framework is not omnipotent where everything matches. If it is wrong, it is wrong.

Caution 3. Orthogonal Does Not Mean Combined

Classical and quantum being orthogonal means "the two are independent." It does not mean to combine them into a single equation.

Wrong approach: time^2 + observer^2 = ? (mixing axes from different brackets)
Correct approach: time^2 + space^2 = c^2 (trade-off only within the same bracket)

Just as you cannot add east and height, classical axes and quantum axes must not be directly computed in a single equation. Each bracket is an independent unit.

Caution 4. What Is Solved and What Remains

All samples follow the same 5 steps.

Example: Think of making pizza -- 1.Knead dough (original equation) 2.Roll into circle (norm substitution) 3.Add toppings (constant substitution) 4.Put in oven (domain transformation) 5.Taste (Verdict). If the order changes, you do not get pizza.

Sample 1. Deriving Time Dilation (Special Relativity)

Step 1. Banya Equation

$$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$

Step 2. Norm Substitution

Since the 4 axes are orthogonal, bundle brackets into norms.

$$\delta^{2} = \|C\|^{2} + \|Q\|^{2}$$
$\|C\|$ = classical bracket norm, $\|Q\|$ = quantum bracket norm

Step 3. Constant Substitution

Insert the speed of light c into the classical bracket norm. The quantum bracket is not used this time, so leave it as is.

$$\|C\|^{2} = c^{2}$$
$$\text{i.e., }time^{2} + space^{2} = c^{2}$$
Speed of light c = 299,792,458 m/s

Step 4. Domain Transformation -- Object Moving at Velocity v

Setting space = v (velocity), time is determined.

time² + v² = c²
time² = c² - v²
time  = √(c² - v²)

Computing the ratio of time:

$$time / c = \sqrt{1 - v^{2}/c^{2}}$$

Step 5. Discovery + Verdict

This is the time dilation formula of special relativity itself.

$$\gamma = 1 / \sqrt{1 - v^{2}/c^{2}}$$
Einstein's Lorentz factor
At rest (v=0): time = c   -- maximum time
At light speed (v=c): time = 0   -- time stops
The faster you go, the slower time becomes

Verdict: PASS -- Inserting only a single constant c yielded special relativity.

Sample 2. Deriving the Uncertainty Principle

Step 1. Banya Equation

$$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$

Step 2. Norm Substitution

$$\delta^{2} = \|C\|^{2} + \|Q\|^{2}$$

This time, only the quantum bracket is used.

$$\|Q\|^{2} = observer^{2} + superposition^{2}$$

Step 3. Constant Substitution

Insert the reduced Planck constant h-bar into the quantum bracket norm.

$$\|Q\|^{2} = \hbar^{2}$$
$$\text{i.e., }observer^{2} + superposition^{2} = \hbar^{2}$$
$\hbar$ = 1.055 × 10⁻³⁴ J·s

Step 4. Domain Transformation -- Trade-off Between Measurement Precision and Superposition Range

observer and superposition trade off on a circle of radius h-bar.

Increase observer -- superposition decreases
Make observation more precise -- range of possible superposition narrows

Converting observer to position measurement precision (related to Delta-x) and superposition to momentum uncertainty (related to Delta-p):

$$\Delta x \times \Delta p \geq \hbar/2$$

Step 5. Discovery + Verdict

This is the Heisenberg uncertainty principle itself.

Full observation (observer = h-bar): superposition = 0 -- superposition vanishes
No observation (observer = 0): superposition = h-bar -- full superposition

Verdict: PASS -- Inserting only a single constant h-bar yielded the uncertainty principle.

TOCTOU Interpretation -- Why the Trade-off

Above we said "observer and superposition trade off." Why? Because h-bar is the radius of the circle? Correct, but there is a deeper reason.

CAS is the operator of the quantum bracket (OPERATOR). A lock must be placed to prevent Status from changing between Compare and Swap. The minimum cost of this lock is h-bar. It has the same structure as a TOCTOU lock in computer science.

Compare position (check Delta-x)
------ momentum may change in between ------
Swap momentum (determine Delta-p)

Lock cost = h-bar/2

If you Compare position precisely (small Delta-x), more lock cost must be spent on position, leaving less for momentum (Delta-p grows). Total cost must be at least h-bar/2. Nothing can be determined at zero cost. This is the true nature of the uncertainty principle.

h-bar is not "a mysterious limit of nature." It is the lock cost that protects Status between Compare and Swap. Computation has a cost. That is obvious.

Relationship between the energy (E_p) and time (t_p) of 1 write:

E_p × t_p = ℏ           ← energy x time of 1 write = h-bar

For n writes:

$$E = n \times m_p \times c^{2} = m \times c^{2}$$
mass $m = n \times m_p$ (number of writes x Planck mass)

Einstein's mass-energy equivalence formula has emerged. Einstein derived this from the invariance of the speed of light. In the Banya Framework, it is derived from the Write Axiom. The paths are different but the destination is the same.

Verdict: PASS -- Inserting 3 constants + 1 hypothesis yielded E = mc^2.

Part 1. Definition and Structure of Banya Framework

Core Claims of This Report

$$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$
delta: change | time: time | space: space | observer: observation | superposition: superposition

The Banya Framework starts from this single equation and claims and verifies the following:

Structure: The universe is a structure where 4 domains (time, space, observer, superposition) are orthogonal. The classical bracket (time+space) is DATA (storage, Foreground), and the quantum bracket (observer+superposition) is OPERATOR (operator, Background). The sum of all physical quantities is the amount of change (delta).

Operator: The sole operator of the universe is CAS (Read, Compare, Swap). 1 CAS operation = quantum of action (h-bar). Equivalence is confirmed across 9 domain transformations. CAS has internal structure in its 3 stages, which structurally matches quark 3 colors, 6 flavors, and 8 gluons.

Write: Write is a real physical phenomenon. CAS ties a knot on all 4 axes (Swap=space, Read=observer, Compare=superposition, When=time). Eviction (LRU) unties the knot. The 4 forces branch from CAS×DATA access patterns, determined by the domain 4-bit pattern (Axiom 1 proposition, H-45). Causality arises from the logical dependency R, C, S of CAS, and an arrow of time emerges when CAS writes to the time axis. Irreversibility is a property of CAS (OPERATOR), not of time (DATA).

Domain transformation: The Banya Framework enforces all 4 domains and monitors them all. When existing physics equations use only some domains, switching to the remaining domains reveals hidden physical quantities. Observation is subordinate to change, and all observations are fundamentally indirect. Decoherence is a CAS commit (Background to Foreground transition).

Unification: CAS × domain pair = 4 forces (H-45). The access pattern is determined by the domain 4-bit pattern (Axiom 1 proposition). Swap+t×s=gravity, strong=CAS atomicity(confinement), Compare+s×{o,sp}=EM, Read+t×{o,sp}=weak. A single LRU queue unifies visible matter (HOT 5%), dark matter (WARM 27%), and dark energy (COLD 68%). Inserting constants yields hidden values like a system of simultaneous equations. Input: 7. Output: 96+. More comes out than goes in.

Verification: Full verification of 118 physics equations, FAIL 0. 6 fundamental physics equations derived from Write Axiom (all 1.000000). Electron charge, Weinberg angle, W/Z mass ratio, Higgs VEV (0.6% Error) derived from CAS cost. Koide Formula 0.0011% Error.

Chapter 1. Starting Point

There is a passage in the Heart Sutra:

"Everything changes except change itself."

The inventor translated this sentence into mathematics. Change (delta) is invariant. The only thing in the universe that does not change is the "fact of change" itself. This became the left-hand side.

The right-hand side consists of 4 independent axes that produce change: time and space from classical physics, observer and superposition from quantum physics. These 4 axes are orthogonal. They each contribute to change independently without needing to be combined.

$$\delta^{2} = (time + space)^{2} + (observer + superposition)^{2}$$
delta: change | time: time | space: space | observer: observation | superposition: superposition

4 words, 1 line, 2 squares. This is the Banya Framework. The Banya Framework enforces all 4 domains (time, space, observer, superposition) and monitors them all. When existing physics equations use only some domains, it forcibly opens the remaining domains to reveal hidden physical quantities.
